<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1909085512467807231"><em>Monday 27 January<br />“7:15 a.m. Hurrah! The wilderness years are over. For four weeks and five days now have been in functional relationship with adult male, thereby proving am not love pariah as recently feared.”</em><br /><br />Lurching from the cappuccino bars of Notting Hill to the blissed-out shores of Thailand, Bridget Jones searches for The Truth in spite of pathetically unevolved men,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1909085512467807231"><em>Monday 27 January<br />“7:15 a.m. Hurrah! The wilderness years are over. For four weeks and five days now have been in functional relationship with adult male, thereby proving am not love pariah as recently feared.”</em><br /><br />Lurching from the cappuccino bars of Notting Hill to the blissed-out shores of Thailand, Bridget Jones searches for The Truth in spite of pathetically unevolved men, insane dating theories, and Smug Married advice ("I'm just calling to say in the potty! In the potty! Well, do it in Daddy's hand then!"). She experiences a zeitgeist-esque Spiritual Epiphany somewhere between the pages of <em>How to Find the Love You Want Without Seeking It</em> ("can self-help books really help self?"), protective custody, and a lightly chilled Chardonnay.<br /><br /><em>Wednesday 5 March<br />“7:08 p.m. Am assured, receptive, responsive woman of substance. My sense of self comes not from other people but... from... myself? That can’t be right.”</em><br /><br />With another devastatingly hilarious, ridiculous, unnervingly accurate take on modern womanhood, Bridget Jones is back.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/851951-lisa" class="user" title="Lisa">Lisa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/856712.Bridget_Jones" title="Paperback 9780330434348" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/851951-lisa?shelf=chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/851951-lisa?shelf=shite" class="actionLinkLite">shite</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/851951-lisa?shelf=2008" class="actionLinkLite">2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer25792080">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11693188534391618412">This book should be retitled as Bridget Jones: The Unnecessary Sequel. Bridget returns as the hapless and can't-get-it-together heroine with plenty of love, work and weight troubles. The first book has a happy ending and I thought that was the end of it. Since it's so successful, of course the author cannot resist conjuring contrived plot lines for Bridget's second adventure. <br /><br />Bridget came across as charming and endearing in the first book but here she becomes annoying and irritating. I (or the r</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11693188534391618412">This book should be retitled as Bridget Jones: The Unnecessary Sequel. Bridget returns as the hapless and can't-get-it-together heroine with plenty of love, work and weight troubles. The first book has a happy ending and I thought that was the end of it. Since it's so successful, of course the author cannot resist conjuring contrived plot lines for Bridget's second adventure. <br /><br />Bridget came across as charming and endearing in the first book but here she becomes annoying and irritating. I (or the readers) love her int he first book because Bridget is not flawless. This makes her a very accessible character. However, the contrived plot lines of this book has managed to create a gratingly stupid Bridget which I cannot empathise with anymore.<br /><br />This is what happens when authors go on beyond the 'happily ever after' last line.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11693188534391618412">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_511991441">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/511991441" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/874959-jennie" class="left imgcol" title="Jennie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1202174529p2/874959.jpg" alt="Jennie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/511991441?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 20, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/874959-jennie" class="user" title="Jennie">Jennie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer511991441">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17454085856131809957"><em>Weight: 867 lbs (due to entire Chipotle burrito bol still sitting in belly), cigarettes 0 (as don’t smoke), alcohol units 1 (responsible glass of red wine, for heart), calories 1557 (if Chipotle nutrition calculator can be trusted)</em><br /><br />Have just finished reading Bridget Jones’s Diary: The Edge of Reason, aka BJD 2: THE DARCY STRIKES BACK. Still working out feelings re: sequel, as original was pure perfection, part of identity, Pride &amp; Prejudice-related (so obviously superior to almost all other w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17454085856131809957"><em>Weight: 867 lbs (due to entire Chipotle burrito bol still sitting in belly), cigarettes 0 (as don’t smoke), alcohol units 1 (responsible glass of red wine, for heart), calories 1557 (if Chipotle nutrition calculator can be trusted)</em><br /><br />Have just finished reading Bridget Jones’s Diary: The Edge of Reason, aka BJD 2: THE DARCY STRIKES BACK. Still working out feelings re: sequel, as original was pure perfection, part of identity, Pride &amp; Prejudice-related (so obviously superior to almost all other works of fiction), etc. Am having trouble reckoning feelings for this novel, as trainwreck of a movie is hanging over head in manner of pinata filled with poo or old, stinky cheeses.<br /><br />Shall not dwell on turd of a movie, however, flawed as it is, because love the lovely book! Like Bridget Jones’s Diary, sequel is based on Jane Austen novel, this time Persuasion. Had not read Persuasion until several years ago and ended up liking just as much (if not more? blasphemy!) as P&amp;P. Naturally, Persuasion suffers from clear lack of Darcy, however Wentworth equally swoon-worthy, also Anne Elliot is obvious patron saint of Singletons everywhere, having been declared old spinster at virginal age of 27.<br /><br />Our little Bridget is still struggling with job, money, romance, family (overbearing mother, drunken father), blah dee blah LIFE in usual ridiculous and fun manner. All old friends characters are back, including urban family (Jude, Shazzer, Tom), Marrieds (Smug and Otherwise), insane boss Richard Finch, delightful mess Daniel Cleaver, and of course Mark Darcy, with whom Bridget is now deeply in love. New characters join Bridget’s world in form of odious Rebecca, a jellyfish (aka frenemy) on the prowl for Bridget’s boyfriend, and friend Magda’s adorable moppets, created to make Bridget look alternately crazy and competent.<br /><br />Do wish that book had not included any romantic turmoil for Bridget and Mark Darcy, however realize that there would have been conspicuous lack of plot otherwise. Could not even bring self to get worked up over ridiculousness of certain plotlines (Thai prison, hole in side of flat, stinky fish left in purse for weeks, what-have-you) because of love for all things Bridget and Darcy, also because of equally important happy ending (spoilers)! Suppose am typical girl that way, heart going all aflutter at any mention of Jones-Darcy reconciliation, evidence of Darcy-still-in-love, etc.<br /><br />Recommend this book for all who enjoyed Bridget Jones’s Diary, or like well-done chick lit (still hate that hateful phrase, should stop using immediately) in general. Especially worth reading for special treat in sequel (as all sequels must one-up original) in form of Colin Firth (aka THE Mr. Darcy) being interviewed by Bridget Jones, which unfolds exactly as one would expect.<br /><br />In short, sequel is v.g.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17454085856131809957">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1429054485">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7883196589604188136">La Fielding se saca de la manga una trama liosa y con muchos altibajos, perdiendo mucha de la gracia y frescura del pirmer libro. Mark Darcy y la madre de Bridget son lo mejor (por favor, la madre es ahostiablemente graciosa). A Bridget a veces la matabas, a veces le dabas un achuchón. Al menos te entretiene y, si lo comparas con la peli, es una maravilla (la peli es es-pan-to-sa -&gt; salvo Colin Firth #AyOmá)</span>

          </span>

  <a href="/user/show/163750-callista" class="left imgcol" title="Callista "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1189653481p2/163750.jpg" alt="Callista " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/206323794?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 29, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/163750-callista" class="user" title="Callista ">Callista </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/35842.Bridget_Jones" title="Paperback 9780143034438" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/163750-callista?shelf=contemp-pop-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">contemp-pop-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer206323794'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer206323794">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11693259385497992842">An unnecessary sequel. Often contrived and unbelievable. Especially the Colin Firth interview, the awful contractor, the Thai drug trafficking disaster, the African visitor, and the romantic difficulties easily solvable by a decent conversation or reading of a note. Bridget does too many things that are idiotic and/or insane. She never thinks to turn that piece of paper over and doesn't even do it accidentally?! She can never learn to get anywhere on time, no matter how important the event? And</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11693259385497992842">An unnecessary sequel. Often contrived and unbelievable. Especially the Colin Firth interview, the awful contractor, the Thai drug trafficking disaster, the African visitor, and the romantic difficulties easily solvable by a decent conversation or reading of a note. Bridget does too many things that are idiotic and/or insane. She never thinks to turn that piece of paper over and doesn't even do it accidentally?! She can never learn to get anywhere on time, no matter how important the event? And it would not have surprised me one bit if it had said on the last page, "...And I woke up in detox and realised Mark Darcy was a figment of my imagination."<br />BUT the reasons for giving this 2 stars instead of one are: the style and quirky catchphrases that had me laughing even when I didn't buy the scenarios, the poking fun at self-help books, and Mark finally punching Daniel.<br /></span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2059203487120268612">Fits of uncontrollable laughter. That would describe me reading this book. What a great followup to the first one! For those of you who have only seen the movie and not read the book, warning: the movie script cuts quite a bit out, and changes quite a bit. For instance, the whole lesbian thing in the movie? Never happened. The "other woman" who Bridget thought was after Mark really was after Mark in the book. Daniel Cleaver barely makes an appearance, just a brief few times, literally only 3 bri</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2059203487120268612">Fits of uncontrollable laughter. That would describe me reading this book. What a great followup to the first one! For those of you who have only seen the movie and not read the book, warning: the movie script cuts quite a bit out, and changes quite a bit. For instance, the whole lesbian thing in the movie? Never happened. The "other woman" who Bridget thought was after Mark really was after Mark in the book. Daniel Cleaver barely makes an appearance, just a brief few times, literally only 3 brief occasions. He was never in Thailand with Bridget and Shaz, as he was in the movie. Therefore, the fight scene with Mark and Daniel never happens...however, he does (Mark) punch him (Daniel) in a later scene, but nothing like the fight in the movie. Also, Mark doesn't go to Thailand to rescue Bridget - he did his work at home and in Dubai to catch Jed. The one thing that amuses me vastly about what they cut out was the fact that Bridget interviews Colin Firth for a freelance newspaper article!!! HA! For obvious reasons, that would have been impossible to have in the movie script, as Colin Firth ended up playing Mark Darcy in the movies. They really, really did leave out A LOT, and this is definitely one of many occasions where the book so surpasses the attempt at the movie. That being said, I love the movie and it's hilarious. It just doesn't match up with the book, and that always pisses me off. It's really too bad that Helen Fielding never came out with a trilogy for this. I would have loved to have had a third book detailing Mark and Bridget getting engaged and married and some crazy stuff happening amidst all of that (the book ends with no engagement). Love, love, love this book!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_46863395">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/46863395" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1132033-stephanie" class="left imgcol" title="Stephanie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1231396341p2/1132033.jpg" alt="Stephanie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/46863395?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 19, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1132033-stephanie" class="user" title="Stephanie">Stephanie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer46863395">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11071180827593587144">After finishing <u>Bridget Jones's Diary</u> for the second time, I turned my attention to <u>Bridge Jones: The Edge of Reason</u>, by Helen Fielding, which I'd never read before. I have to say that with both books, there were definitely laugh-out-loud moments, although there were more with <u>Edge of Reason</u> than <u>Diary</u>.<br /><br />I'm embarrassed to admit it took me at least to the middle of the book to realize that this book was a take-off of <u>Persuasion</u>. And once again, I admire Ms. Fielding's facility in translating a cla</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11071180827593587144">After finishing <u>Bridget Jones's Diary</u> for the second time, I turned my attention to <u>Bridge Jones: The Edge of Reason</u>, by Helen Fielding, which I'd never read before. I have to say that with both books, there were definitely laugh-out-loud moments, although there were more with <u>Edge of Reason</u> than <u>Diary</u>.<br /><br />I'm embarrassed to admit it took me at least to the middle of the book to realize that this book was a take-off of <u>Persuasion</u>. And once again, I admire Ms. Fielding's facility in translating a classic to the modern age. Before I picked up this book, I wondered, idly, "<u>Pride and Prejudice</u> ended with a marriage. What on earth is Helen Fielding going to do in her sequal?" I assumed it would be one more of those books written by Jane Austen devotees who cannot stand not knowing what happens next, where Elizabeth and Darcy, happily married, turn detective, or where Elizabeth, happily married, works on getting Georgiana married off. Turning to <u>Persuasion</u> for inspiration was felicitous.<br /><br />In <u>Persuasion</u>, Anne Elliott and Captain Wentworth loved each other in their youth (fully ten years ago), but were driven apart by the machinations and bad advice of Anne's family. At the end of the book, happily, they have reconciled and their love is as strong as ever. In <u>Edge of Reason</u>, Bridget and Mark have been together for a full four weeks before they are driven apart by a series of misunderstandings, the machinations of vicious Rebecca (an exceedingly well-drawn character), and the bad advice (at least, in Mark's opinion) that Bridget has gleaned from the self-help books that comprise her library. Well done, Ms. Fielding -- I think that's a wonderful way to begin a sequal and also an inspired retelling of a classic.<br /><br />This book was great fun and brought me great joy reading it. I think Ms. Fielding's satirical pen has sharpened somewhat. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11071180827593587144">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_572055961">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/572055961" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4420232-pam-geemul" class="left imgcol" title="Pam Geemul "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442863577p2/4420232.jpg" alt="Pam Geemul " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/572055961?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 05, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4420232-pam-geemul" class="user" title="Pam Geemul ">Pam Geemul </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer572055961">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2763190720573190355">It took me so long time to finish the book because I hated it. Totally and absolutely HATED it. Wanted to dispose of the book midway but convinced myself to go through it because I had flicker of hope that it might get better. But alas, I was so wrong. Bridget Jones must be one of the shallowest, most superficial characters I ever came across. One CANNOT have her life centered around losing weight and indulging in self pity for the simple reason that one has no boyfriend. Seriously, on nearly ev</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2763190720573190355">It took me so long time to finish the book because I hated it. Totally and absolutely HATED it. Wanted to dispose of the book midway but convinced myself to go through it because I had flicker of hope that it might get better. But alas, I was so wrong. Bridget Jones must be one of the shallowest, most superficial characters I ever came across. One CANNOT have her life centered around losing weight and indulging in self pity for the simple reason that one has no boyfriend. Seriously, on nearly every single page of the book, Bridget makes reference to the weight that she needs to lose, and the fear of dying single. What is so wrong with that I wonder if one has to end up with a total fuckwit, as she herself puts it? Her friends are no less shallow and except from drinking, smoking and talking about how to get your hands on a boyfriend, they do not have anything else to say. Bridget has a good job, which unfortunately she is bad at (but does not do anything to improve her performance) a flat, a car, friends, a loving family- that is, everything that a smart, modern, independent woman would like to achieve and be grateful for, but what does she do? Moan and whine that she has no man and this, she does throughout the book. I am very unforgiving I know, but there is only so much nonsense I can put up with from an apparently ‘modern and independent’ woman. <br />The book is also not funny in the least and there are a lot of cringe-moments. I gather that the author wanted to create the character of an average woman with whom many will recognize themselves, but this is sooo not the case. <br />I think it is important for me to point out here that I am NOT a man-hater, bra-burning feminist.<br />I do enjoy reading about the so called average women and on several occasions I do recognize myself in them- clumsily going through life and making the most of what is being thrown their way. In one way or the other, the women always endeavor to better their lives. However here Bridget permanently indulges in this self pity and you can’t help from feeling bored and angry with her. <br />Moreover Bridget’s mother comes as a racist. Sorry, but this is unacceptable. Bringing an “tribal man” from Africa to the UK and parading him like an object is NOT FUNNY. It’s racist AND nasty. <br />Helen Fielding based this book on Persuasion by Jane Austen- the same Jane Austen who through her books advocated the emancipation of women, and who chose to remain happily single rather than marry for convenience. As such, I am sure I will not be exaggerating if I say that Jane Austen must be incensed wherever she is. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2763190720573190355">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_52466446">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52466446" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie" class="left imgcol" title="PurplyCookie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1415491715p2/2214498.jpg" alt="PurplyCookie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/52466446?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 25, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie" class="user" title="PurplyCookie">PurplyCookie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/35842.Bridget_Jones" title="Paperback 9780143034438" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=romance-novel" class="actionLinkLite">romance-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer52466446">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13425916167856167924">This is probably the one rare time I'd say that a book's sequel is much better than its predecessor. <br /><br />In this continuation of her diary, Bridget again recounts the ups and downs of the single life, coupled by the indifference shown to her by Mark Darcy, her now established boyfriend. <em>"Hurrah! The wilderness years are now over. For four weeks and five days now have been in functional relationship with adult male, thereby proving am not love pariah as recently feared." </em> Add to Darcy's indifference</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13425916167856167924">This is probably the one rare time I'd say that a book's sequel is much better than its predecessor. <br /><br />In this continuation of her diary, Bridget again recounts the ups and downs of the single life, coupled by the indifference shown to her by Mark Darcy, her now established boyfriend. <em>"Hurrah! The wilderness years are now over. For four weeks and five days now have been in functional relationship with adult male, thereby proving am not love pariah as recently feared." </em> Add to Darcy's indifference the arrival of Rebecca, who absolutely has no girlfriend code of ethics when it comes to poaching another woman's man.<br /><br /><em>Whole dating world is like hideous game of bluff and double bluff with men and women firing at each other from opposite lines of sandbags. Is as if there is a set of rules that you are supposed to be sticking to, but no one knows what they are so everyone just makes up their own. Then you end up getting chucked because you didn't follow the rules correctly, but how could you be expected to, when you didn't know what they were in the first place? </em><br /><br />Everything else also proves to be topsy-turvy, as Bridget's mother has returned from a trip to Kenya with a young Masai in tow, to her father's consternation; her best friends Jude, Shazzer, and Tom are all trapped in dating hell themselves; her apartment has a gaping hole thanks to an unreliable carpenter; an ex-boyfriend (Daniel Cleaver) has just reentered her life; and now someone is sending Bridget death threats--could it be Mark Darcy as the detectives suspected?<br /><br />Bridget is a slightly silly person, a bit on the unrealistic side (who knew that she had practically bought almost the entire section of self-help books of a bookstore?), but I suppose diaries (as the format of this novel proves) may include ones ultimate unrealistic fantasies (like being rescued by Colin Firth or Prince William). While Bridget is on the edge of reason, her on-again off-again boyfriend is the voice of reason and the perfect comic foil.<br /><br /><br /><u>Book Details: </u><br /><br /><u>Title</u> Bridget Jones: The Edge of Reason <br /><u>Author</u> Helen Fielding<br /><u>Reviewed By</u> Purplycookie</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13425916167856167924">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_101991656">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101991656" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/872174-swissmiss" class="left imgcol" title="Swissmiss"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1202138756p2/872174.jpg" alt="Swissmiss" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/101991656?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 09, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/872174-swissmiss" class="user" title="Swissmiss">Swissmiss</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/578597.The_Edge_of_Reason" title="Paperback 9780330367356" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer101991656">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10474395042914276196">The great thing about this book is that it completely preserved the tone, voice, characterizations, and humor of the first Bridget Jones book. It is easy to read but not dumbed-down. In fact, the nearly telegraphic style makes the reader work just a bit harder than she is used to, in order to divine the meaning. So that's all good. Why, then, have I given this sequel only three stars, where the first book received five?<br /><br />There were three things that led me to this decision... and at one point, I w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10474395042914276196">The great thing about this book is that it completely preserved the tone, voice, characterizations, and humor of the first Bridget Jones book. It is easy to read but not dumbed-down. In fact, the nearly telegraphic style makes the reader work just a bit harder than she is used to, in order to divine the meaning. So that's all good. Why, then, have I given this sequel only three stars, where the first book received five?<br /><br />There were three things that led me to this decision... and at one point, I was even hovering at two stars, but there was some redemption toward the end.<br /><br />First, I felt myself not liking Bridget much in certain parts. In the first book, although obviously flawed, she was still very likable, and even easy to identify with. I think that is in fact the main reason for the success of this series, that Bridget's personality and experiences strike a chord with an entire generation of women who see themselves in her. Well, when Bridget started dumping on Mark, just to please her girlfriends, and being inexcusably stupid, neglectful, and incompetent at work, she lost completely any sympathy she had with me. Bridget is at her best when being mortified at her mother bringing home a Kikuyu from her African safari, or suffering when she sees her boyfriend being fawned over by a gorgeous, rich, thin rival. Even when she pitches off-the-wall, slightly embarrassing or shallow ideas for Sit Up Britain, and things don't quite pan out the way she expected. But when she has a big interview with Colin Firth and acts like a thirteen-year-old schoolgirl (if that), and then doesn't even bother to write the article afterward, her unlucky bumbling turns into flat-out incompetence that makes me wonder what redeeming qualities she could possibly have. And she doesn't have a clue where Germany is? Germany! <br /><br />Okay. Moving on. The next peeve I had was that it felt like the author was stretching too far, coming up with outlandish plots, possibly in order to make it play better on the big screen. Getting caught for drug-smuggling in Thailand is just so far out of the scope of a normal thirty-something single girl's experience that it just didn't fit for me. And then the whole stalker thing with the builder? It felt so last-minute and stuck together. <br /><br />The last thing I didn't much like was the fact that Bridget never saw Mark's message on the back of the poem (and why would he have written on the back of a poem anyway? Surely there was a blank piece of paper around). I mean, come on, she was in a prison for a week with no other reading material, and she took the poem out and re-read it several times. She would have noticed something on the back. This may seem like a minor detail, but it was actually a pretty big point for drawing out the uncertainty over their relationship right up to the end. There were a couple of other things, too, like the fact that there was a gaping hole in the wall of Bridget's house for months, and no one said anything... and she didn't need to get a building permit for the addition, either. I just felt like there was too much suspension of disbelief necessary, that things could never have happened like that in the real world. That might not be a huge drawback for some books, but Bridget Jones' success banks on the reader being able to place themselves in Bridget's place, and for these things to actually happen to them (or someone they know, or someone who at least lives on the same planet). <br /><br />Now, what is the redeeming quality that brought this back up from 2 stars? It's the fact that Bridget does actually seem to learn something. She actually does make some major changes in her life (throwing out all of her self-help books, quitting her job), and sees that she was wrong to treat Mark the way she did. She gains insight into her character and acts on that. I was also very touched by the mother-daughter scene near the end, where Bridget's mother actually seems to come down to Earth for a few minutes and gives some very good, profound advice. <br /><br />So, in the end, I did like this book, and I can admire the author's skill in writing and creating a worthwhile piece of entertainment. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10474395042914276196">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_528814499">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/528814499" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/17229950-chase-a" class="left imgcol" title="Chase A"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Chase A" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/528814499?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 07, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/17229950-chase-a" class="user" title="Chase A">Chase A</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer528814499">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11424139820691918152">Bridget Jones: The Edge of Reason, a fictional work of British literature by Helen Fielding, is a whirlwind of a romance set in the city of Notting Hill. Bridget, the calorie, cigarette, and alcohol obsessed thirty year old, finds herself in unfortunate relationships that hardly ever work out for her. But eventually, she finds the man of her dreams, Mark Darcy. It has been “four weeks and five days [that she has] been in a functional relationship with an adult male,” portraying that she is not a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11424139820691918152">Bridget Jones: The Edge of Reason, a fictional work of British literature by Helen Fielding, is a whirlwind of a romance set in the city of Notting Hill. Bridget, the calorie, cigarette, and alcohol obsessed thirty year old, finds herself in unfortunate relationships that hardly ever work out for her. But eventually, she finds the man of her dreams, Mark Darcy. It has been “four weeks and five days [that she has] been in a functional relationship with an adult male,” portraying that she is not a crazy repulse of love (Fielding 3). But not everything goes in her favor throughout their relationship. Mark begins talking about a woman he works with more and more in front of Bridget, and Bridget becomes over-worried and extremely jealous. She constantly thinks the worst about her relationship with her perfect man. The two English soul mates seems like the perfect couple, however, with some bumps along the way, Mark and Bridget break up, which puts Bridget in a state of depression. Will Bridget ever convince Mark that he’s the only one she loves? Or will she never make it back together with Mark, the man of her dreams? <br />	Helen Fielding makes the reader feel like they are one of Bridget’s best friends through all of her unmanageable boy troubles. Fielding wrote this book with an intention of making the characters easy to identify with and communicate with. Her writing, quick and relatable, helps the reader cultivate an understanding for Bridget and her “said-so”, irreplaceable, connection with Mark Darcy. There is no way you can not be fixated to this book and the dynamic characters placed in the British work. <br />	In Bridget and Mark’s relationship, anything can be expected. The main point of the work is to point out that anyone can find love, even if it seems impossible. Bridget makes this clear, as someone who believes she is a repellant of love. No one ever knows what will happen between the two unpredictable characters, as a couple. However, if you want to know what the fate is of this couple, you will have to read Bridget Jones: The Edge of Reason. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11424139820691918152">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer385911881">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8027597394819769869">Helen Fielding is basically the world's greatest feminist. In her first Bridget Jones book, she taught us that no woman is complete unless she has the love of a foppish, sub-Hugh Grant, barely heterosexual posh man to complete her. To add to the confusion, Bridget is in love with the actor Colin Firth, who they end up casting in the film as her actual love interest, Mark Darcy. If that wasn't confusing enough, they throw in Hugh actual Grant as the Bad Boy Whom All Women Are Attracted To In Spit</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8027597394819769869">Helen Fielding is basically the world's greatest feminist. In her first Bridget Jones book, she taught us that no woman is complete unless she has the love of a foppish, sub-Hugh Grant, barely heterosexual posh man to complete her. To add to the confusion, Bridget is in love with the actor Colin Firth, who they end up casting in the film as her actual love interest, Mark Darcy. If that wasn't confusing enough, they throw in Hugh actual Grant as the Bad Boy Whom All Women Are Attracted To In Spite Of Themselves. And he doesn't really play a Hugh Grant type either. Well, he does, but it's more like the Hugh Grant in About A Boy. Or the Hugh Grant in real life, who fucks crack whores in the mouth.<br /><br />This is a review of the book though, which is not a film. It's not the first book either, it's the sequel to the first book. And it's not the film which is a sequel to the first film. In this book, Bridget gets her dream job, interviewing Colin Firth for some magazine or TV show or whatever. This is very confusing if you've seen the first film, obviously. This is the book though, so we'll carry on.<br /><br />Does anything of note happen in this book? LOADS of stuff, but none that I can actually remember. There's a scene at the start of it which is funny because foreign people are hilarious, and gay people are icky. I think that's the point the author was trying to make, anyway. The key themes of the book are that women are useless without men, other women stab you in the back at every opportunity, and that no one thin or good looking can be a good person.<br /><br />Fielding's novels are loosely based on a couple of Jane Austen books, although they're not that much like them; well, except for the fact that their attitudes to women, men and relationships are two hundred years out of date.<br /><br />Can't wait for the third one!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1337937076">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1337937076" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/45135661-marlowe" class="left imgcol" title="Marlowe"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1437153715p2/45135661.jpg" alt="Marlowe" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1337937076?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/45135661-marlowe" class="user" title="Marlowe">Marlowe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1337937076">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16998588674658569672">I am often typecast by friends and family as “the one who likes books.” To non-readers, a book is a book is a book, so I often end up getting some really weird books that I would never pick up for myself. This is how I ended up in possession of The Edge of Reason, Helen Fielding’s second Bridget Jones novel.<br /><br />In this novel, Bridget stumbles through her day-to-day life, surviving one ridiculous mishap after another, until she is finally reunited with her love.<br /><br />The writing is designed to imitate a fo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16998588674658569672">I am often typecast by friends and family as “the one who likes books.” To non-readers, a book is a book is a book, so I often end up getting some really weird books that I would never pick up for myself. This is how I ended up in possession of The Edge of Reason, Helen Fielding’s second Bridget Jones novel.<br /><br />In this novel, Bridget stumbles through her day-to-day life, surviving one ridiculous mishap after another, until she is finally reunited with her love.<br /><br />The writing is designed to imitate a form of shorthand that might be used to keep a diary. It reminded be somewhat of Flowers for Algernon in the sense that the form was an important part of the content (something that we (should) see often in poetry, but that is quite a bit rarer in novels). It was interesting and it gave the story quite a bit of verisimilitude. The short sentences kept me reading at a faster pace than I do normally, which was rather interesting. And even though I read this about four years ago, I still use the “v.” (or “vee,” if I’m speaking) as a shorthand for “very.”<br /><br />Bridget Jones herself is a hilariously inept character, bouncing from one situation to another with little agency of her own. I have a soft spot for such characters, so long as they aren’t annoying about it, so I rather enjoyed her as well. The situations themselves were so ridiculous (particularly the one involving a naked boy and a bunny – yes, really) that they had me laughing quite a bit as I read through.<br /><br />This is the ice-cream of the reading world – it’s enjoyable, not particularly nutritious, but it won’t rot your brain out either (provided it’s consumed only sparingly and interspersed with meatier fare).</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16998588674658569672">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9454038087792220465">I really enjoyed this book, even though it was virtually no where near how its portrayed in the movie!!! I have to say I am disappointed that the Mark Darcy from the books isn't exactly represented in the movies, he is much more funny and fucked up and sexual than the movies give him credit for!!! Its all good though, the book was hilarious all the same and once again, I wanted to tackle Bridget's ass and slap some sense into her for all her neurotic behavior!!!! Being done with this book now brings me to the next book in the series, which is how I started reading the books in the first place-WHOOP WHOOP! I of course, would suggest this book to anyone who's a fan of Bridget, or Fitzwilliam Darcy-Mark Darcy-Colin Firth, LMAO, as Bridget is very obsessed with all the above, and rightfully so! Damn that Colin Firth is a handsome charming devil of tall British hotness! OMG, am behaving as a non-British black American version of Bridget where everything comes back to Colin Firth and Pride and Prejudice (which I do have on DVD along with Bridget Jones' Diary and Edge of Reason, don't hate)!!! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9454038087792220465">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_819078092">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/819078092" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/415420-tara" class="left imgcol" title="Tara"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1373156170p2/415420.jpg" alt="Tara" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/819078092?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 10, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/415420-tara" class="user" title="Tara">Tara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/685426.Bridget_Jones" title="Hardcover 9780670892969" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer819078092">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14337455538209402226">Despite the fact that now that I'm reading this as an adult, I'm much more highly critical of Bridget's extreme shallowness and idiocy... this book is still an enjoyable read. Last time I read it, I was around 20, so I'm more in a place now to identify with Bridget. <br /><br />It's been over 10 years since I last read it, and I was delighted to find one thing I'd forgotten: like the first book with Pride &amp; Prejudice, this plot is loosely based on Jane Austen's <em>Persuasion</em>. If you're not a Jane Austen fa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14337455538209402226">Despite the fact that now that I'm reading this as an adult, I'm much more highly critical of Bridget's extreme shallowness and idiocy... this book is still an enjoyable read. Last time I read it, I was around 20, so I'm more in a place now to identify with Bridget. <br /><br />It's been over 10 years since I last read it, and I was delighted to find one thing I'd forgotten: like the first book with Pride &amp; Prejudice, this plot is loosely based on Jane Austen's <em>Persuasion</em>. If you're not a Jane Austen fanatic, it might not be entirely obvious--but elements of <em>Persuasion</em> are definitely there, right down to the lovesick Benwick. Brilliant. <br /><br />The plot is held together with what I might call the Meg Cabot Conundrum, in that nearly every single problem in Bridget's life could be solved if she just chose to communicate. Case in point, her breakup with Mark Darcy is 100% due to lack of communication--just saying the simple words "Hey, I want to stay together because I love you" would have worked. BAM, problem solved. So all right, the problems are mainly a bit flimsy and you want to bash Bridget over the head with a Milk Tray throughout the book for not just using the brain you <em>know</em> she has (more because of the first book than this one, sadly) and trying to solve her own problems.<br /><br />And yet, I'm still sucked in, entertained, amused, and delighted when Bridget does ultimately find happiness. What can I say: I'm still a sucker for Bridget.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14337455538209402226">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3090.Helen_Fielding">About Helen Fielding</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/3090.Helen_Fielding"><img alt="3090" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1381158323p2/3090.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer9654268316224104865">Helen Fielding was born in Yorkshire. She worked for many years in London as a newspaper and TV journalist, travelling as wildly and as often as possibly to Africa, India and Central America. She is the author of four novels: Cause Celeb, Bridget Jones’ s Diary, Bridget Jones:The Edge of Reason and Olivia Joules and the Overactive Imagination, and co-wrote the screenplays for the movie of Bridget</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9654268316224104865">Helen Fielding was born in Yorkshire. She worked for many years in London as a newspaper and TV journalist, travelling as wildly and as often as possibly to Africa, India and Central America. She is the author of four novels: Cause Celeb, Bridget Jones’ s Diary, Bridget Jones:The Edge of Reason and Olivia Joules and the Overactive Imagination, and co-wrote the screenplays for the movie of Bridget Jones’s Diary and the sequel based on The Edge of Reason. She now works full-time as a novelist and screenwriter and lives in London and Los Angeles. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9654268316224104865">...more</a>

    </div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/8140-bridget-jones-the-edge-of-reason">Quotes from The Edge of Reason</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“Keep thinking back about what Mum said about being real and the Velveteen Rabbit book (though frankly have had enough trouble with rabbits in this particular house). My favorite book, she claims of which I have no memory was about how little kids get one toy that they love more than all the others, and even when its fur has been rubbed off, and it's gone saggy with bits missing, the little child still thinks it's the most beautiful toy in the world, and can't bear to be parted from it.<br /><br />That's how it works, when people really love each other, Mum whispered on the way out in the Debenhams lift, as if she was confessing some hideous and embarrassing secret. But, the thing is, darling, it doesn't happen to ones who have sharp edges, or break if they get dropped, or ones made of silly synthetic stuff that doesn't last. You have to be brave and let the other person know who you are and what you feel.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/104699-keep-thinking-back-about-what-mum-said-about-being-real" class="actionLinkLite">93 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“9p.m. My flat. Feel very strange and empty. Is all very well thinking everything is going to be different when you come back but then it is all the same. Suppose I have to make it different. But what am I going to do with my life? <br /> I know. Will eat some cheese.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/113788-9p-m-my-flat-feel-very-strange-and-empty-is-all" class="actionLinkLite">76 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a href="/work/quotes/8140-bridget-jones-the-edge-of-reason" style="float: right" class="actionLink">More quotes…</a>
